Soldier's Will:
GPS: 50.36363, -4.139505
Rank: Musician
Name: James Paul Meehan
Regiment: H.Q. Coy. 138th Infantry Regiment, 35th Division, U.S. Army
Died: 27/09/1918
Type (No.): Died (1450734)
Age: 26
Enlisted: Missouri, U.S.A.
Commemorated: National Cemetery, Arlington, Virginia, U.S.A.
Further Details: Son of Mary Anne Meehan (nee McNamara) and John Meehan, 91 Carey's Road., Limerick. During the period from April 1920 through July 1921, the remains of over 2,000 U.S. Servicemen buried in Europe during World War I were interred in Arlington National Cemetery, Specifically in Section18. Through the efforts of the Argonne Unit American Women's Legion, the Argonne Cross was erected to their memory and in their honour. It is situated in the southwest corner of Section 18 and faces east. A grove of 19 pine trees is on three sides of the Cross (north, south and west). These trees are symbolic of the Argonne Forest where many of the men fought and died. James Paul was the brother-in-law of Andrew Joyce, 8106, R.M.F., KIA 9/8/15

Rank: Gunner
Name: Henry Alphonsus Torpey
Regiment: 8th Bn. Australian Field Artillery
Died: 05/06/1917
Type (No.): KIA (20109)
Age: 33
Enlisted: East Melbourne, Victoria, Australia
Commemorated: Strand Military Cemetery, Comines-Warneton, Belgium
Further Details: Son of John and Catherine Torpey, Limerick. Henry emigrated to Australia at the age of 13. He joined his brother Joseph and resided at 376 Albert St., East Melbourne, where he attended St. Patrick's College. After finishing school he was employed by Victoria Railways. Henry enlisted on 9th December 1915 and was killed in action on 5th June 1917 near Ploegsteert in the Ypres Salient.
